<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Shops">Shops</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sainsbury%27s&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Shops">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In May 2018 Sainsbury's shop portfolio was as follows.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<table class="wikitable" style="margin: 0 auto 0 auto;">

<tbody><tr>
<th>Format
</th>
<th>Number
</th>
<th>Total Space (sq ft)
</th></tr>
<tr>
<td>Supermarkets
</td>
<td>608
</td>
<td>21,296,000
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>Convenience shops
</td>
<td>806
</td>
<td>1,913,000
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>Total
</td>
<td>1,423
</td>
<td>23,209,000
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>According to <a href="/wiki/CACI" title="CACI">CACI</a>, as of 2006, Sainsbury's has market dominance in 8 postcode areas; <a href="/wiki/TQ_postcode_area" title="TQ postcode area">TQ</a> (<a href="/wiki/Torquay" title="Torquay">Torquay</a>), <a href="/wiki/SN_postcode_area" title="SN postcode area">SN</a> (<a href="/wiki/Swindon" title="Swindon">Swindon</a>), <a href="/wiki/GU_postcode_area" title="GU postcode area">GU</a> (<a href="/wiki/Guildford" title="Guildford">Guildford</a>), <a href="/wiki/RH_postcode_area" title="RH postcode area">RH</a> (<a href="/wiki/Redhill,_Surrey" title="Redhill, Surrey">Redhill</a>), <a href="/wiki/DA_postcode_area" title="DA postcode area">DA</a> (<a href="/wiki/Dartford" title="Dartford">Dartford</a>), <a href="/wiki/SE_postcode_area" title="SE postcode area">SE</a> (<a href="/wiki/South_East_(London_sub_region)" class="mw-redirect" title="South East (London sub region)">South East London</a>), <a href="/wiki/EN_postcode_area" title="EN postcode area">EN</a> (<a href="/wiki/London_Borough_of_Enfield" title="London Borough of Enfield">Enfield</a>) and <a href="/wiki/WV_postcode_area" title="WV postcode area">WV</a> (<a href="/wiki/Wolverhampton" title="Wolverhampton">Wolverhampton</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>It is particularly strong in London and the South-East, where it is based, and has powerful positions within many UK cities. The company acquired the Midlands-based Thoroughgood in the 1930s. Expansion since 1945 has given the company national reach, although the chain is not as well-represented in Scotland as Tesco, and Morrisons (as Safeway dominated Scotland before being taken over by them). This is partly due to Sainsbury's having lost out to Tesco in the bidding war for <a href="/wiki/William_Low" title="William Low">William Low</a> in the 1990s.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Supermarkets">Supermarkets</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sainsbury%27s&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Supermarkets">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sainsbury%27sCropped.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Sainsbury%27sCropped.jpg/220px-Sainsbury%27sCropped.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="198" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Sainsbury%27sCropped.jpg/330px-Sainsbury%27sCropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Sainsbury%27sCropped.jpg/440px-Sainsbury%27sCropped.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1517" data-file-height="1365" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sainsbury%27sCropped.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Interior of Sainsbury's <a href="/wiki/Gloucester_Quays" title="Gloucester Quays">Gloucester Quays</a> shop</div></div></div>
<p>On 29 September 2010, Sainsbury's opened one of its largest UK shops, an extension of its existing shop in Crayford, South East London, which now has over 100,000&#160;sq&#160;ft (9,300&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) of retail space and is its largest supermarket to be built in the UK. Bybrook in Ashford Kent, which reopened on 16 November 2011 has over 100,000&#160;sq&#160;ft (9,300&#160;m<sup>2</sup>).<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The refurbished <a href="/wiki/Lincoln,_Lincolnshire" class="mw-redirect" title="Lincoln, Lincolnshire">Lincoln, Lincolnshire</a> shop opened on 24 November 2010 making it the UK's second largest Sainsbury's supermarket after Crayford at 98,712&#160;sq&#160;ft (9,170.6&#160;m<sup>2</sup>).<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Shops in the 'supermarket' category all have similar layouts and operations but may vary in their offering to the customer. Most will have a convenience kiosk, produce, meat, fish, groceries and frozen food, and manned and <a href="/wiki/Self-service_checkouts" class="mw-redirect" title="Self-service checkouts">self-service checkouts</a>. However depending on the size of the shop they may also have an in-shop bakery, butcher, fishmonger, delicatessen and pizza counters, a cafe, TU clothing, general merchandise, petrol station and online picking department. Some shops also feature concessions such as a beauty hall, travel agents, <a href="/wiki/Jessops" title="Jessops">Jessops</a>, <a href="/wiki/Patisserie_Valerie" title="Patisserie Valerie">Patisserie Valerie</a>, <a href="/wiki/Specsavers" title="Specsavers">Specsavers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carte_D%27or" class="mw-redirect" title="Carte D&#39;or">Carte D'or</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ben_and_Jerrys" class="mw-redirect" title="Ben and Jerrys">Ben and Jerrys</a> ice cream stands, <a href="/wiki/Zizzi" title="Zizzi">Zizzi</a> pizza counters,  Sushi Gourmet counters, juice bars, The Fragrance Shop, <a href="/wiki/Argos_(retailer)" title="Argos (retailer)">Argos</a> and <a href="/wiki/Habitat_(retailer)" title="Habitat (retailer)">Habitat</a>. Others also feature a "Centre for Dentistry" where dental treatments are offered and/or an "Explore Learning" centre where children are offered extra English and maths tuition. Some shops also feature a <a href="/wiki/Starbucks_Coffee" class="mw-redirect" title="Starbucks Coffee">Starbucks Coffee</a> instead of an in-shop cafe.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="Sainsbury.27s_Fuel"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Sainsbury's_Fuel">Sainsbury's Fuel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sainsbury%27s&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Sainsbury&#039;s Fuel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Sainsbury's operates a chain of fuel forecourts located at some of its supermarkets selling diesel, petrol and City Diesel. The chain first opened a forecourt in 1974 at its <a href="/wiki/Croydon" title="Croydon">Croydon</a> SavaCentre hypermarket, the forecourts were initially supplied by and marketed as <a href="/wiki/Jet_(brand)" title="Jet (brand)">Jet</a> stations.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> However, from 1980 onwards Sainsbury's operated its own forecourts and sourced its own fuel. In 2004 <a href="/wiki/BP" title="BP">BP</a> became the supplier of fuel and operated its forecourts at supermarkets where possible. This deal ended in 2009 and operation of all forecourts and fuel sourcing returned to the control of Sainsbury's.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="Sainsbury.27s_Caf.C3.A9"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Sainsbury's_Café">Sainsbury's Café</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sainsbury%27s&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Sainsbury&#039;s Café">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>A number of stores operate self-service cafes, marketed as Sainsbury's Café, of which most are open for almost as long as the shops are open.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Sainsbury.27s_Local"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Sainsbury's_Local">Sainsbury's Local</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sainsbury%27s&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Sainsbury&#039;s Local">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sainsbury%27s_Local" title="Sainsbury&#39;s Local">Sainsbury's Local</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bournemouth_,_Winton_-_Sainsbury%27s_Local_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1289750.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Bournemouth_%2C_Winton_-_Sainsbury%27s_Local_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1289750.jpg/220px-Bournemouth_%2C_Winton_-_Sainsbury%27s_Local_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1289750.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Bournemouth_%2C_Winton_-_Sainsbury%27s_Local_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1289750.jpg/330px-Bournemouth_%2C_Winton_-_Sainsbury%27s_Local_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1289750.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Bournemouth_%2C_Winton_-_Sainsbury%27s_Local_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1289750.jpg/440px-Bournemouth_%2C_Winton_-_Sainsbury%27s_Local_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1289750.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bournemouth_,_Winton_-_Sainsbury%27s_Local_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1289750.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sainsbury's Local in <a href="/wiki/Winton,_Dorset" title="Winton, Dorset">Winton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bournemouth" title="Bournemouth">Bournemouth</a></div></div></div>
<p>As well as developing its own sites, Sainsbury's expanded its convenience portfolio through acquisitions of <a href="/wiki/Bell%27s_Stores" class="mw-redirect" title="Bell&#39;s Stores">Bell's Stores</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jackson%27s_Stores" class="mw-redirect" title="Jackson&#39;s Stores">Jackson's Stores</a>, JB Beaumont and SL Shaw Ltd. Sainsbury's initially retained the strong Bells, Jacksons and Beaumont branding. For example, refurbished shops were called <i>Sainsbury's at Bells</i>. These were effectively Sainsbury's Local shops with a revised fascia, retaining some features of the former local chain. Unrefurbished shops retained the original brand and logo, but still offered Sainsbury's own brand products, pricing and some point of sale, without accepting Nectar cards. The old websites were also retained with some Sainsbury's branding. However all of these acquired shops were fully converted to the Local fascia from 4 May 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In July 2013, chief executive Justin King announced plans to focus on expanding its convenience shops to surpass the number of its supermarket properties by 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Sainsbury.27s_Online"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Sainsbury's_Online">Sainsbury's Online</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sainsbury%27s&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Sainsbury&#039;s Online">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sainsbury%27s_Online" title="Sainsbury&#39;s Online">Sainsbury's Online</a></div>
<p>Sainsbury's operates an internet shopping service branded as "Sainsbury's Online". To use this service customers choose their groceries online, or by phone (which includes a "phone order" fee).<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> Sainsbury's also provide the Sainsbury's Gift Cards and Sainsbury's Business Direct transactional websites that sell gift cards, gift vouchers and food tokens with credit or value that can be spent at any Sainsbury shop. Both products are not valid for buying certain products or services. The Gift Card website promotes the card as an ideal gift due to the large range of products and the number of shops available to spend them in. The Business Direct website, operated by MBL Solutions Ltd, promotes the cards as ideal for rewarding and motivating employees.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Distribution">Distribution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sainsbury%27s&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Distribution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Distribution_centre_(J_Sainsbury%27s).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Distribution_centre_%28J_Sainsbury%27s%29.jpg/220px-Distribution_centre_%28J_Sainsbury%27s%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="173" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Distribution_centre_%28J_Sainsbury%27s%29.jpg/330px-Distribution_centre_%28J_Sainsbury%27s%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Distribution_centre_%28J_Sainsbury%27s%29.jpg/440px-Distribution_centre_%28J_Sainsbury%27s%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1901" data-file-height="1494" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Distribution_centre_(J_Sainsbury%27s).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sainsbury's <a href="/wiki/Distribution_center" title="Distribution center">distribution centre</a> in Waltham Point</div></div></div>
<p>Sainsbury's supply chain operates from 13 regional distribution centres (RDCs), with two national distribution centres for slower moving goods, and two frozen food facilities. In addition, the depot at Tamworth transships general merchandise to the RDCs.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dt>Regional distribution centres</dt></dl>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Basingstoke,_Hampshire" class="mw-redirect" title="Basingstoke, Hampshire">Basingstoke, Hampshire</a></li>
<li>Belfast, <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dartford,_Kent" class="mw-redirect" title="Dartford, Kent">Dartford, Kent</a></li>
<li>Emerald Park, Emerson's Green, <a href="/wiki/Bristol" title="Bristol">Bristol</a></li>
<li>Greenford, London</li>
<li>Vauxhall, Nine Elms (<a href="/wiki/London_SW8" class="mw-redirect" title="London SW8">London SW8</a>)</li>
<li>Hams Hall, Coleshill, <a href="/wiki/West_Midlands_(county)" title="West Midlands (county)">West Midlands</a></li>
<li>Haydock, <a href="/wiki/St_Helens,_Merseyside" title="St Helens, Merseyside">St Helens, Merseyside</a></li>
<li>Langlands Park, East Kilbride, <a href="/wiki/South_Lanarkshire" title="South Lanarkshire">South Lanarkshire</a></li>
<li>Northampton, <a href="/wiki/Northamptonshire" title="Northamptonshire">Northamptonshire</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sherburn,_North_Yorkshire" title="Sherburn, North Yorkshire">Sherburn, North Yorkshire</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/St_Albans,_Hertfordshire" class="mw-redirect" title="St Albans, Hertfordshire">St Albans, Hertfordshire</a></li>
<li>Waltham Point, <a href="/wiki/Essex" title="Essex">Essex</a></li></ul>
<dl><dt>Regional distribution centres – Slow Moving</dt></dl>

<li><a href="/wiki/Stoke,_Staffordshire" class="mw-redirect" title="Stoke, Staffordshire">Stoke, Staffordshire</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tamworth,_Staffordshire" title="Tamworth, Staffordshire">Tamworth, Staffordshire</a></li></ul>
<dl><dt>Regional distribution centres – Frozen</dt></dl>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Elstree" title="Elstree">Elstree</a>, Hertfordshire</li></ul>
<dl><dt>National Distribution Centre – General Merchandise</dt></dl>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Daventry,_Northamptonshire" class="mw-redirect" title="Daventry, Northamptonshire">Daventry, Northamptonshire</a></li></ul>
<dl><dt>National Distribution Centre – Clothing</dt></dl>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Bedford,_Bedfordshire" class="mw-redirect" title="Bedford, Bedfordshire">Bedford, Bedfordshire</a></li>
<li>Shire Park, Worcestershire</li></ul>
<p>A planned regional distribution centre (RDC) in Exeter was abandoned, and the land sold to Lidl.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Subsidiaries">Subsidiaries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sainsbury%27s&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Subsidiaries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span id="Sainsbury.27s_Bank"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Sainsbury's_Bank">Sainsbury's Bank</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sainsbury%27s&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Sainsbury&#039;s Bank">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sainsbury%27s_Bank" title="Sainsbury&#39;s Bank">Sainsbury's Bank</a></div>
<p>In 1997 Sainsbury's Bank was established – a joint venture between J Sainsbury plc and the <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_Scotland" title="Bank of Scotland">Bank of Scotland</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> later a part of the <a href="/wiki/Lloyds_Banking_Group" title="Lloyds Banking Group">Lloyds Banking Group</a>. Services offered include car, life, home, pet and travel insurance as well as health cover, loans, credit cards, savings accounts and <a href="/wiki/Individual_Savings_Account" title="Individual Savings Account">Individual Savings Accounts</a>. On 8 May 2013, Sainsbury's announced it would buy the 50% share in the business owned by Lloyds Banking Group.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Sainsbury.27s_Energy"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Sainsbury's_Energy">Sainsbury's Energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sainsbury%27s&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Sainsbury&#039;s Energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Founded in 2011, Sainsbury's Energy is a virtual utility provider in partnership with <a href="/wiki/Npower_(United_Kingdom)" title="Npower (United Kingdom)">nPower</a> who offer gas and electricity. Sainsbury's no longer have face-to-face salespersons in-shop but there are leaflets and posters etc. advertising Sainsbury's Energy in its supermarkets.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> Sainsbury's Energy was previously supplied by <a href="/wiki/British_Gas" title="British Gas">British Gas</a>; the agreement ended in 2019 with nPower commencing supply from February.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Former_formats_and_ventures">Former formats and ventures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sainsbury%27s&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Former formats and ventures">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<dl><dt>Sainsbury's Freezer Centres</dt></dl>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sainsbury%27s_Freezer_Centres" title="Sainsbury&#39;s Freezer Centres">Sainsbury's Freezer Centres</a></div>
<p>Sainsbury's Freezer Centres were a frozen food chain operated between 1974 and 1986, the shops were entirely dedicated to frozen food. Due to competition from specialist frozen food chains such as Bejam, Sainsbury's converted its original service shops that were too small for modern use to small frozen specialist shops. Despite initial difficulty as only 11% of the population owned a freezer, the chain expanded to 21 shops at its height. As freezers became more popular, frozen food departments were designed into Sainsbury's main supermarkets, and the chain was sold to <a href="/wiki/Bejam" title="Bejam">Bejam</a> in 1986, who were ultimately sold to <a href="/wiki/Iceland_(supermarket)" title="Iceland (supermarket)">Iceland</a> in 1989.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dt>Sainsbury's SavaCentre</dt></dl>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/SavaCentre" title="SavaCentre">SavaCentre</a></div>
<p>SavaCentre was a chain of 13 hypermarkets and 7 discount supermarkets operated between 1977 and 2005, initially in a joint venture with <a href="/wiki/British_Home_Stores" title="British Home Stores">BHS</a>. The shops ranged in size between 66,000&#160;sq&#160;ft (6,100&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) and 117,000&#160;sq&#160;ft (10,900&#160;m<sup>2</sup>), and the discount supermarkets between 31,000&#160;sq&#160;ft (2,900&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) and 70,000&#160;sq&#160;ft (6,500&#160;m<sup>2</sup>). At the time of its inception it was the only dedicated hypermarket chain in the UK. Shop layout consisted of a 50:50 split between food and non-food shopping, with a complete range of both retailers' products, and later included input from <a href="/wiki/Habitat_(retailer)" title="Habitat (retailer)">Habitat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mothercare" title="Mothercare">Mothercare</a> as they merged with BHS. Some shops also included features such as a petrol station and in-shop cafe. In 1989 Sainsbury's bought out BHS's half stake, but still allowed BHS to retail from SavaCentres until they offered its own clothing and merchandise offering.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dt>Sainsbury's Calais Wine Shop</dt></dl>
<p>Sainsbury's operated one alcohol hypermarket in partnership with <a href="/wiki/Auchan" title="Auchan">Auchan</a> in <a href="/wiki/Calais" title="Calais">Calais</a>, France for the lucrative UK <a href="/wiki/Booze_cruise" title="Booze cruise">booze cruise</a> market. The shop closed in 2010 after describing the operation as 'economically unviable'.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dt>Sainsbury's Market</dt></dl>
<p>In 2002 Sainsbury's opened an experimental shop in the <a href="/wiki/Bluebird_Garage" title="Bluebird Garage">Bluebird Building</a> in <a href="/wiki/Chelsea,_London" title="Chelsea, London">Chelsea</a>, London. The concept of the 'Market' shop was to provide a large range of fresh meat, fish, delicatessen items and bread through colleagues serving over counters. Colleagues were specially hired for their skill and passion for their roles in-shop. The layout also provided a larger than usual area for retailing fresh produce. The shop closed in 2004 after poor results.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> A second, much larger version in <a href="/wiki/Pimlico" title="Pimlico">Pimlico</a> was designated as a 'Market' shop, but the shop's branding and layout was gradually reverted to a standard Sainsbury's shop.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dt>Fresh Kitchen</dt></dl>
<p>In 2011 Sainsbury's opened a trial <a href="/wiki/Snack_food" class="mw-redirect" title="Snack food">food to go</a> shop in Fleet Street London selling sandwiches, baguettes and hot snacks in an effort to expand its business into new areas of opportunity. The shop closed a year later, after the shop's lease was not renewed. Sainsbury's commented that footfall was too high to offer high standards of quality and service however it was not ruling out performing another trial in another location, explaining that it had learnt a lot.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dt>Mobile by Sainsbury's</dt></dl>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mobile_by_Sainsbury%27s" title="Mobile by Sainsbury&#39;s">Mobile by Sainsbury's</a></div>
<p>Sainsbury's operated a virtual mobile network from 2001 until 2003 which closed due to being commercially unsustainable. In 2013 Sainsbury's re-entered the UK telecommunications industry when it launched a mobile phone network called Mobile by Sainsbury's.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Mobile_virtual_network_operator" title="Mobile virtual network operator">virtual network</a> was operated in partnership with <a href="/wiki/Vodafone" title="Vodafone">Vodafone</a>. The network was promoted heavily in-shop and most supermarkets started retailing <a href="/wiki/Subscriber_identity_module" class="mw-redirect" title="Subscriber identity module">SIM cards</a> and handsets for the network. However, in 2015 Sainsbury's announced that the service would be closing in January 2016 after a breakdown in the relationship with its provider Vodafone.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dt>Sainsbury's Compare and Save</dt></dl>
<p>Sainsbury's Compare and Save was a comparison and switching service website that promoted a wide range of television, broadband and telephone deals from a variety of providers. The service, free to Sainsbury's customers, claimed to list 15,000 different packages. The website and service launched in 2008 and was operated by <a href="/w/index.php?title=SimplifyDigital&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="SimplifyDigital (page does not exist)">SimplifyDigital</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dt>Sainsbury's Pharmacy</dt></dl>
<p>Sainsbury's operated 270 pharmacies within its supermarkets.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> Sainsbury's was also a provider of outpatient hospital pharmacy services, operating pharmacies at three major UK hospitals: <a href="/wiki/Guy%27s_Hospital" title="Guy&#39;s Hospital">Guy's Hospital</a>, <a href="/wiki/St_Thomas%27_Hospital" title="St Thomas&#39; Hospital">St Thomas' Hospital</a> and <a href="/wiki/James_Cook_University_Hospital" title="James Cook University Hospital">James Cook University Hospital</a>. In July 2015 Sainsbury's announced they were selling their 281 pharmacies to <a href="/wiki/Lloydspharmacy" class="mw-redirect" title="Lloydspharmacy">Lloydspharmacy</a> for £125 million in 2016 with all 2500 pharmacy employees being transferred over and new rent agreements being made.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dt>Sainsbury's Entertainment</dt></dl>
<p>Sainsbury's Entertainment was a transactional website which provided films as downloads or for streaming, using <a href="/wiki/Rovi_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Rovi Corporation">Rovi Corporation</a> software.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> The site arranged to register with <a href="/wiki/ATVOD" title="ATVOD">ATVOD</a> as a <a href="/wiki/Video_on_demand" title="Video on demand">video on demand</a> service.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> The website also sold MP3 downloads as well as eBooks through <a href="/wiki/ANobii" title="ANobii">aNobii</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> The site began operating in 2010 and until March 2014 also sold physical products including DVDs, CDs, Blu-ray discs and books. These were posted to the customer by a distributor, which after 2011 was Sainsbury's subsidiary company: Global Media Vault Ltd.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> Customers received nectar points from shopping at Sainsbury's Entertainment.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> Sainsbury's announced in September 2016 that it would close the business on 30 November 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dt>Sainsbury's Euro Garages Partnership</dt></dl>
<p>Sainsbury's trialed franchising their convenience store format to <a href="/wiki/Euro_Garages" class="mw-redirect" title="Euro Garages">Euro Garages</a> who planned to operate six small stores within its service stations, the first time Sainsbury's has trusted a third party to operate a Sainsbury's store. Beginning in <a href="/wiki/Blackburn" title="Blackburn">Blackburn</a> in 2016 Sainsbury's re-trained EuroGarages staff of 15 to operate the convenience store and later followed with stores in <a href="/wiki/Heathrow" class="mw-redirect" title="Heathrow">Heathrow</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bury,_Greater_Manchester" title="Bury, Greater Manchester">Bury</a>. In February 2018 Sainsbury's issued a statement calling a mutual end to the trial: "following a commercial review, a joint decision has been made to bring the trial to a close." <sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Product_ranges">Product ranges</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sainsbury%27s&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Product ranges">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>A large shop typically stocks around 30,000 lines of which around 20% are "own-label" goods. These own-brand lines include:
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sainsbury%27s_Basics.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Sainsbury%27s_Basics.JPG/250px-Sainsbury%27s_Basics.JPG" decoding="async" width="250" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Sainsbury%27s_Basics.JPG/375px-Sainsbury%27s_Basics.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Sainsbury%27s_Basics.JPG/500px-Sainsbury%27s_Basics.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="2112" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sainsbury%27s_Basics.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The own label Basics range is its low cost products</div></div></div>
<table class="wikitable" style="margin: 0 auto 0 auto;">

<tbody><tr>
<th>Name
</th>
<th>Description
</th></tr>
<tr>
<td><i><a href="/wiki/Value_brands_in_the_United_Kingdom#Sainsbury&#39;s_Basics" title="Value brands in the United Kingdom">Basics</a></i>
</td>
<td>An economy range of around 700 lines, mainly food but also including other areas such as toiletries and stationery. The Basics range uses minimal packaging with simple orange and white designs. Sainsbury's Local shops sell none or very few of these lines.
<p>Equivalent to <a href="/wiki/Tesco" title="Tesco">Tesco</a>'s <i>Everyday Value</i>, <a href="/wiki/Asda" title="Asda">Asda</a>'s <i>Smart Price</i> and <a href="/wiki/Morrisons" title="Morrisons">Morrisons</a>' <i>M Savers</i>.
</p><p>Additional product lines were added in late 2013, together with new packaging.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><i>by Sainsbury's</i>
</td>
<td><span id="by_Sainsbury&#39;s"></span>All own-brand food products that are not part of any of the other ranges (over 6,500 different lines) have been re-branded as "<i>by</i> Sainsbury's". This was first introduced on frozen foods in late 2010, and the re-branding was completed in January 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><i>Taste The Difference</i>
</td>
<td>Premium-quality brand containing around 1100 food lines, including many processed foods such as ready-made meals and premium bakery lines. The range consisting of 1141 lines was re-launched in September 2010 when 75% of the range was improved or newly added.
<p>Similar to <a href="/wiki/Asda" title="Asda">Asda</a>'s <i>Extra Special</i>, <a href="/wiki/Tesco" title="Tesco">Tesco</a>'s <i>Finest</i> and <a href="/wiki/Morrisons" title="Morrisons">Morrisons</a>' <i>The Best</i>.
</p>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><i>Be Good To Yourself</i>
</td>
<td>Products with reduced calorific and/or fat content. The BGTY range was relaunched in January 2010.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><i>My Goodness!</i>
</td>
<td>Similar to the BGTY range, 'My Goodness!' is a range of healthy foods from Sainsbury's.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><i>Deliciously FreeFrom</i>
</td>
<td>Launched in 2002, it has over 75 product lines. These products are all grouped together in one aisle of the shop (except fresh and frozen lines).<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> These products are suitable for those allergic to <a href="/wiki/Dairy" title="Dairy">dairy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wheat" title="Wheat">wheat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gluten" title="Gluten">gluten</a> (although some are free from wheat/gluten but contain dairy). The range was relaunched in September 2016 as Deliciously FreeFrom, the range has also doubled in offer with now over 150 lines.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><i>SO Organic</i>
</td>
<td>Around 500 lines of food and drink which are derived from sources produced in accordance with organic standards.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><i>Tu</i>
</td>
<td>The own-brand clothing range, which had a full re-brand in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><i>Sainsbury's HOME</i>
</td>
<td>A range of home products, such as lighting, rugs, and kitchen products. This range has now been rolled out to most shops stocking non-food ranges. After the success of its own brand range, Sainsbury's will rebrand this range into the 'by Sainsbury's' range in August 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> In 2017, Sainsbury's started to re-branded all its non-food offering, excluding clothing as 'Sainsbury's HOME'.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><i>Home Collection</i>
</td>
<td>A range of quality home products, such as cutlery, crockery, kitchenware and bed linen. Uses the same typeface and logo as Taste the Difference.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><i>On The Go</i>
</td>
<td>A new range of sandwiches, salads and snacks launched in September 2016, this new range replaced all of the existing sandwiches and replaced with improved and new fillings. Burritos, Pasta Pots and Sushi are included in the range as well as a selection of snacks.
</td></tr></tbody></table>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Marketing_and_branding">Marketing and branding</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sainsbury%27s&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Marketing and branding">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Shop_fascias">Shop fascias</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sainsbury%27s&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Shop fascias">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Since 1869 Sainsbury's used various fascias using the title 'J Sainsbury'. This was replaced in 1999 by simply: 'Sainsbury's'. The flagship supermarket in <a href="/wiki/Greenwich" title="Greenwich">Greenwich</a>, South London, first trialled the new look, leading to the term 'Greenwich Blue', which was used to describe the signature colour of new identity. After its success most supermarkets were refurbished with dark blue walls, bright orange wall panels and grey shelving, as well as new checkouts. Individual counters also had different, brightly coloured panels behind them. Gradually the format was rolled out across the entire Sainsbury's estate. The 'Greenwich Blue' look has been phased out and new supermarkets now have a fresher look.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> Old external signage bearing the 'J Sainsbury' name was still to be found in use as recently as summer 2011 in Swindon, Ashbourne in Derbyshire and Blackheath, West Midlands.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nectar_loyalty_card">Nectar loyalty card</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sainsbury%27s&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Nectar loyalty card">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Nectar_loyalty_card" title="Nectar loyalty card">Nectar loyalty card</a></div>
<p>Sainsbury's was a founding member of the UK's largest retail loyalty scheme called 'Nectar' in 2002. The scheme allows customers to earn points on almost everything bought from Sainsbury's as well as from other participating retailers in return for a large range of rewards. For every pound spent the customer earns 1 point - a reward equivalent to 0.5% of supermarket purchases. Since 2015 Sainsbury's no longer offers 1 bonus point for every carrier bag the customers reuses.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>From April 2015, Sainsbury's halved the number of points that customers earned for every pound, to one point per pound.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> Sainsbury's previously operated Sainsbury's Reward Scheme between 1995 and 2002 where customers used 'Reward Cards' or 'Storecards' to earn and spend points in a similar way, but limited to Sainsbury's businesses.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 1 February 2018 Sainsbury's announced that it had acquired all assets, colleagues, systems and licences required for the full and independent operation of the Nectar loyalty programme in the UK through the acquisition of the shares of <a href="/wiki/Aimia_(company)" title="Aimia (company)">Aimia Inc's</a> UK business for £60m.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Sainsbury.27s_Active_Kids"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Sainsbury's_Active_Kids">Sainsbury's Active Kids</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sainsbury%27s&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Sainsbury&#039;s Active Kids">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sainsbury%27s_Active_Kids" title="Sainsbury&#39;s Active Kids">Sainsbury's Active Kids</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Active_Kids.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Active_Kids.JPG/250px-Active_Kids.JPG" decoding="async" width="250" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Active_Kids.JPG/375px-Active_Kids.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Active_Kids.JPG/500px-Active_Kids.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="2112" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Active_Kids.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Sainsbury's Active Kids banner outside a school. Tokens are collected at supermarkets, and are redeemed for sports equipment.</div></div></div>
<p>Until 2017, Sainsbury's ran an annual voucher scheme for local organisations to redeem against equipment for sports and other activities. Customers earned vouchers from their shopping which they donated to an organisation of their choice, who then redeemed the vouchers with Sainsbury's, crediting their account with points to spend on items from a catalogue.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Brand_match">Brand match</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sainsbury%27s&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Brand match">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2011 Sainsbury's introduced brand match. It matched prices of competitors. In March 2014 it stopped matching prices in <a href="/wiki/Tesco" title="Tesco">Tesco</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> In August 2015 it rolled out the match pricing online.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> In April 2016 it stopped the brand match completely allowing customers to use the vouchers for two weeks after the offer closed. <a href="/wiki/Tesco" title="Tesco">Tesco</a> took Sainsbury's brand match vouchers for two months after the offer finished.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Brand_ambassadors">Brand ambassadors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sainsbury%27s&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Brand ambassadors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>2000–2011: <a href="/wiki/Jamie_Oliver" title="Jamie Oliver">Jamie Oliver</a> was the public face of Sainsbury's, appearing on television and radio advertisements and in-shop promotional material. The deal earned him an estimated £1.2&#160;million every year. In the first two years of these advertisements were estimated to have given Sainsbury's an extra £1&#160;billion of sales or £200&#160;million gross profit.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>2010–2017: Paralympic swimmer <a href="/wiki/Ellie_Simmonds" title="Ellie Simmonds">Ellie Simmonds</a> was a Sainsbury's Active Kids ambassador.<sup id="cite_ref-marketingmagazine.co.uk_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-marketingmagazine.co.uk-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>2012–2014: Former footballer <a href="/wiki/David_Beckham" title="David Beckham">David Beckham</a> was a Sainsbury's Active Kids ambassador, in a deal that was claimed to be worth over £3.5 million.<sup id="cite_ref-marketingmagazine.co.uk_200-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-marketingmagazine.co.uk-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Slogans">Slogans</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sainsbury%27s&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Slogans">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Sainsbury's currently uses the "Live Well For Less" slogan which was launched on 15 September 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup> Over the years, Sainsbury's has used many slogans:
</p>
<ul><li><i>"Quality perfect, Prices Lower"</i> – The slogan used on the shop-front of the Islington shop in 1882.</li>
<li><i>"Sainsbury's For Quality, Sainsbury's For Value"</i> – Used in 1918 above the Drury Lane shop.</li>
<li><i>"Sainsbury's. Essentials for the Essentials.</i>"</li>
<li><i>"Good Food Costs Less At Sainsbury's"</i> – Used from the 1960s to the 1990s. Described by BBC News as "probably the best-known advertising slogan in retailing."<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><i>"Sainsbury's – Everyone's Favourite Ingredient"</i> – Used in a series of TV commercials in the 1990s which featured celebrities cooking Sainsbury's food.</li>
<li><i>"Fresh food, fresh ideas. Eat healthy"</i> – Used in 1998.</li>
<li><i>"Value to shout about"</i> – A 1998/1999 campaign fronted by <a href="/wiki/John_Cleese" title="John Cleese">John Cleese</a> which was widely claimed to have been a major mistake. Sainsbury's said it actually depressed sales. However, the company had been losing sales for years because of the rise of Tesco.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><i>"Making Life Taste Better"</i> – Introduced 1998 and used until May 2005.</li>
<li><i>"Try something new today"</i> – Introduced in September 2005 until September 2011.</li>
<li><i>"Value where it matters"</i> – Used in advertising from late 2010 until May 2011.</li>
<li><i>"Clothes You Can't Wait To Wear"</i> – Used in all new advertising for TU Clothing as part of advertising campaign throughout May 2011.</li>
<li><i>"Live Well For Less"</i> – Introduced in September 2011 following an 18-month business review.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><i>"Christmas is for Sharing"</i> – Used for all Sainsburys' Christmas adverts from 2013 to present.</li>
<li><i>"Here's to Extraordinary"</i> – Used only throughout 2012 to promote sponsorship of the <a href="/wiki/London_2012_Paralympic_Games" class="mw-redirect" title="London 2012 Paralympic Games">London 2012 Paralympic Games</a>.</li></ul>
<p>Sainsbury's was a sponsor of the <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Paralympics" title="2012 Summer Paralympics">Paralympic Summer Games</a> in London 2012, and it was the largest sponsorship signing in the history of the Games.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Street_name">Street name</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sainsbury%27s&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Street name">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>When Sainsbury's opened its new supermarket in <a href="/wiki/Kingston_upon_Thames" title="Kingston upon Thames">Kingston upon Thames</a> on part of the site of the former <a href="/wiki/Kingston_Power_Station,_London" title="Kingston Power Station, London">Kingston Power Station</a> in the 2000s, a decision was made to name a new road leading to the supermarket "Sury Basin", a pun on the name of "Surrey" (Kingston's historic county) but in fact an <a href="/wiki/Anagram" title="Anagram">anagram</a> of the company's name.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Staffing">Staffing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sainsbury%27s&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Staffing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In 2013, Sainsbury's won the Employer of the Year at the Oracle Retail Week Awards.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2010, Sainsbury's opened seven food colleges that teach fishmongery, butchery, breadmaking and confectioning. 21,000 colleagues have been trained at these venues so far.<sup id="cite_ref-j-sainsbury.co.uk_211-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-j-sainsbury.co.uk-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup> Qualifications can be gained through in house training, and so far 15,400 colleagues have been awarded <a href="/wiki/City_and_Guild" class="mw-redirect" title="City and Guild">City and Guild</a> qualifications.<sup id="cite_ref-j-sainsbury.co.uk_211-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-j-sainsbury.co.uk-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Our Sainsbury's is a social and information website for colleagues to use to access colleague benefits and information, and to interact with other colleagues.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Sainsbury's graduate scheme called '2020 Leaders' aims to recruit and develop potential leaders for the most senior roles of the company.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Employee_relations">Employee relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sainsbury%27s&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Employee relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<dl><dt>Great Place to Work Group</dt></dl>
<p>Each supermarket or group of conveniences shops elects a group of 'representatives' from across their shop or region to meet once a month to discuss the working life of their branch and the company. The meetings can include communication from Head Office, the chance to organise charity or local events and the opportunity for employee's to discuss issues and feedback or question the attending Store Manager. The group controls a budget for donating to local charities and a budget for investing in employee facilities. The group was previously known as the 'Colleague Council', a separate version for young employees was called 'Youth Forum' and another separate group called 'SSA Council' existed to organise events in shops. A change in 2014 combined all three into 'Great Place To Work Groups'. The shop groups are part of a national structure, meeting monthly at shops and depots, then monthly at a regional level and then finally at a national meeting less frequently. The shop level is chaired by Store Managers, regional level by a Store Manager and Regional Operations Manager and nationally by the Groups HR Director.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-j-sainsbury.co.uk_211-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-j-sainsbury.co.uk-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dt>Sainsbury's Staff Association</dt></dl>
<p>Sainsbury's Staff Association was founded in 1947. It is owned and run by the colleagues of Sainsbury's. Any permanent colleague can join at a cost of £1 every 28 days for one person (or £1.20 every 28 days for two people). The funds raised are collected into accounts in every shop, and spent on whatever the shops SSA colleagues wish, usually social events and experiences out of shop. Benefits also include further discounts with other retailers.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dt>Sainsbury's Veterans Association</dt></dl>
<p>Sainsbury's Veterans Association was started in 1947 by 8 colleagues who wished all colleagues to stay in touch with each other. Today members enjoy a range of benefits including Honorary SSA membership, 10% discount, newsletters, invitation to an annual reunion, a visitor service, birthday and anniversary gifts, donation upon bereavement and transfer of benefits to spouse upon death. To qualify colleagues have to serve 25 years with the company. The association's presidents are former Sainsbury's CEO and later Chairman <a href="/wiki/Lord_Sainsbury_of_Preston_Candover_KG" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord Sainsbury of Preston Candover KG">Lord Sainsbury of Preston Candover KG</a> and former Sainsbury's CEO Dino Adriano.<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversies">Controversies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sainsbury%27s&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Controversies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Price_fixing">Price fixing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sainsbury%27s&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Price fixing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2007 Sainsburys was fined for its involvement in a dairy price-fixing cartel along with other large retailers and processors.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tax_avoidance">Tax avoidance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sainsbury%27s&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Tax avoidance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A number of companies including Sainsbury's used a scheme to avoid <a href="/wiki/VAT" class="mw-redirect" title="VAT">VAT</a> by forcing customers paying by card to unknowingly pay a 2.5% 'card transaction fee', though the total charged to the customer remained the same. Such schemes came to light after <a href="/wiki/HMRC" class="mw-redirect" title="HMRC">HMRC</a> litigated against <a href="/wiki/Debenhams" title="Debenhams">Debenhams</a> over the scheme during 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Online_only_recruitment">Online only recruitment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sainsbury%27s&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Online only recruitment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In November 2007, Sainsbury's became the first major British employer to introduce an "internet only" staff recruitment system. At the time, it was estimated that the move would save the company £4 million a year in administration costs.<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup> This move came at a time when approximately half of the British adult population was estimated to have access to the internet at home, though by 2010 it was estimated that more than 80% of the adult population had internet access.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Treatment_of_overseas_workers">Treatment of overseas workers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sainsbury%27s&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Treatment of overseas workers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In a 2006 report the British anti-poverty charity <a href="/wiki/War_on_Want" title="War on Want">War on Want</a> criticised the conditions faced by Kenyan workers supplying Sainsbury's with cut flowers.<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Food_safety_prosecutions">Food safety prosecutions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sainsbury%27s&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Food safety prosecutions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Sainsbury's supermarkets have been prosecuted, on more than one occasion, for selling food past its <a href="/wiki/Use_by_date" class="mw-redirect" title="Use by date">use by date</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-fine_229-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fine-229">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup> Evidence also showed that some staff were not correctly trained to carry out their duties involving food safety.<sup id="cite_ref-fine_229-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fine-229">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Removal_of_kosher_products">Removal of kosher products</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sainsbury%27s&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Removal of kosher products">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2014, a photograph surfaced on <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a> showing that the <a href="/wiki/Holborn" title="Holborn">Holborn</a> Sainsbury's franchise responded to anti-Semitic threats by removing kosher products from its shelves.<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup> Complaints began appearing on social media that removing food that is consistent with Jewish dietary restrictions and is produced all over the world was an act of discrimination against Jews.<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup> In response to the negative publicity, the kosher products were restored to the shelves and the staffer who removed them was reprimanded.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Singhsbury.E2.80.99s_shop"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Singhsbury’s_shop">Singhsbury’s shop</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sainsbury%27s&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Singhsbury’s shop">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2012, Jel Singh Nagra, a shop keeper from North Tyneside, was threatened with legal action from Sainsbury's after he named his shop Singhsbury's. It complained about the logo design and the name. Several Singhsbury's are run around the country but none received a threat. Nagra changed the shop name to Morrisinghs. <a href="/wiki/Morrisons" title="Morrisons">Morrisons</a> wished him well.<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Environmental.2Fethical_issues"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental/ethical_issues">Environmental/ethical issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sainsbury%27s&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Environmental/ethical issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In May 2017 Sainsbury's was criticised, including by organisations such as <a href="/wiki/Oxfam" title="Oxfam">Oxfam</a> for dropping its Fairtrade label from tea. Oxfam said it was very unclear as to how Sainsbury's own standards would be higher than those of <a href="/wiki/Marque" class="mw-redirect" title="Marque">Marque</a>'s.<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup> The MD of <a href="/wiki/Divine_Chocolate" title="Divine Chocolate">Divine Chocolate</a>, an ethical trading company part-owned by tens of thousands of cocoa farmers in Ghana said that this move was tipping the balance back in favour of the retailers.<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In January 2018 customers questioned the need to cover coconuts with a plastic film forcing CEO Mike Coupe to state that he would be investigating the issue.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Inequality_in_pricing">Inequality in pricing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sainsbury%27s&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Inequality in pricing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In January 2018, Sainsbury's were found to be charging 50p more for a Valentine's Day card for husbands than for wives. Sainsbury's responded, claiming that a pricing error was to blame.<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Bristol_Rovers_F.C._v_Sainsbury.27s"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Bristol_Rovers_F.C._v_Sainsbury's"><i>Bristol Rovers F.C. v Sainsbury's</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sainsbury%27s&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Bristol Rovers F.C. v Sainsbury&#039;s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Sainsbury's won a bidding process in March 2012 and agreed on a £30m deal to buy <a href="/wiki/Bristol_Rovers_F.C." title="Bristol Rovers F.C.">Bristol Rovers F.C.</a>'s 12,000-capacity <a href="/wiki/Memorial_Stadium_(Bristol)" title="Memorial Stadium (Bristol)">Memorial Stadium</a> in north <a href="/wiki/Bristol" title="Bristol">Bristol</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup> lease it back for a peppercorn rent until the new ground was ready and then redevelop the old stadium as a new shop. The club hoped the money from the sale would largely finance a new <a href="/wiki/UWE_Stadium" title="UWE Stadium">UWE Stadium</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>However Sainsbury's ended up locked in a legal battle with Bristol Rovers<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup> after the chain pulled out of the deal. Sainsbury's argued at the High Court in London that it was legally entitled to terminate the contract because conditions linked to the agreement had not been satisfied. Lawyers for the club said that either the contract "is still on foot" or Sainsbury's had breached it.<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>It was claimed in court that Sainsbury's had been looking for a way out of the deal for nearly two years. David Matthias QC, speaking for the club, said the proposed Sainsbury's supermarket had become "less financially viable" amid a difficult trading climate. He said Sainsbury's saw the restrictions on delivery times as an opportunity to get out of the contract and "did nothing" from January 2014 to challenge the restrictions and get suitable planning permission.<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup> The club successfully made its own application to lift the restrictions in December that year.<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Sainsbury's won its High Court battle after judge Mrs. Justice Proudman ruled that "Sainsbury's must succeed" because the construction of a schedule to the agreement "seems like an insuperable barrier" to the club winning the case.<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In a statement, Rovers accused Sainsbury's of breaking its promises. It described the decision as a 'kick in the teeth' for the people of Bristol. The club claimed that it was "abundantly clear throughout the case that Sainsbury's reneged on its promises to the local community to invest in the region and showed a flagrant disregard for the terms of the contract."<sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Archive">Archive</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sainsbury%27s&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Archive">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Sainsbury's archive of over 16,000 items relating to the business since its foundation is now kept at the <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_London" title="Museum of London">Museum of London</a>. The archive is particularly rich in the product packaging, advertising and retail shop areas.<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
